     1	// Copyright 2017 The Bazel Authors. All rights reserved.
     2	// Use of this source code is governed by a BSD-style
     3	// license that can be found in the LICENSE file.
     4	
     5	// Package resolve defines a name-resolution pass for Starlark abstract
     6	// syntax trees.
     7	//
     8	// The resolver sets the Locals and FreeVars arrays of each DefStmt and
     9	// the LocalIndex field of each syntax.Ident that refers to a local or
    10	// free variable.  It also sets the Locals array of a File for locals
    11	// bound by top-level comprehensions and load statements.
    12	// Identifiers for global variables do not get an index.
    13	package resolve // import "go.starlark.net/resolve"
    14	
    15	// All references to names are statically resolved.  Names may be
    16	// predeclared, global, or local to a function or file.
    17	// File-local variables include those bound by top-level comprehensions
    18	// and by load statements. ("Top-level" means "outside of any function".)
    19	// The resolver maps each global name to a small integer and each local
    20	// name to a small integer; these integers enable a fast and compact
    21	// representation of globals and locals in the evaluator.
    22	//
    23	// As an optimization, the resolver classifies each predeclared name as
    24	// either universal (e.g. None, len) or per-module (e.g. glob in Bazel's
    25	// build language), enabling the evaluator to share the representation
    26	// of the universal environment across all modules.
    27	//
    28	// The lexical environment is a tree of blocks with the file block at
    29	// its root. The file's child blocks may be of two kinds: functions
    30	// and comprehensions, and these may have further children of either
    31	// kind.
    32	//
    33	// Python-style resolution requires multiple passes because a name is
    34	// determined to be local to a function only if the function contains a
    35	// "binding" use of it; similarly, a name is determined to be global (as
    36	// opposed to predeclared) if the module contains a top-level binding use.
    37	// Unlike ordinary top-level assignments, the bindings created by load
    38	// statements are local to the file block.
    39	// A non-binding use may lexically precede the binding to which it is resolved.
    40	// In the first pass, we inspect each function, recording in
    41	// 'uses' each identifier and the environment block in which it occurs.
    42	// If a use of a name is binding, such as a function parameter or
    43	// assignment, we add the name to the block's bindings mapping and add a
    44	// local variable to the enclosing function.
    45	//
    46	// As we finish resolving each function, we inspect all the uses within
    47	// that function and discard ones that were found to be function-local. The
    48	// remaining ones must be either free (local to some lexically enclosing
    49	// function), or top-level (global, predeclared, or file-local), but we cannot tell
    50	// which until we have finished inspecting the outermost enclosing
    51	// function. At that point, we can distinguish local from top-level names
    52	// (and this is when Python would compute free variables).
    53	//
    54	// However, Starlark additionally requires that all references to global
    55	// names are satisfied by some declaration in the current module;
    56	// Starlark permits a function to forward-reference a global or file-local
    57	// that has not
    58	// been declared yet so long as it is declared before the end of the
    59	// module.  So, instead of re-resolving the unresolved references after
    60	// each top-level function, we defer this until the end of the module
    61	// and ensure that all such references are satisfied by some definition.
    62	//
    63	// At the end of the module, we visit each of the nested function blocks
    64	// in bottom-up order, doing a recursive lexical lookup for each
    65	// unresolved name.  If the name is found to be local to some enclosing
    66	// function, we must create a DefStmt.FreeVar (capture) parameter for
    67	// each intervening function.  We enter these synthetic bindings into
    68	// the bindings map so that we create at most one freevar per name.  If
    69	// the name was not local, we check that it was defined at module level.
    70	//
    71	// We resolve all uses of locals in the module (due to load statements
    72	// and comprehensions) in a similar way and compute the file's set of
    73	// local variables.
    74	//
    75	// Starlark enforces that all global names are assigned at most once on
    76	// all control flow paths by forbidding if/else statements and loops at
    77	// top level. A global may be used before it is defined, leading to a
    78	// dynamic error. However, the AllowGlobalReassign flag (really: allow
    79	// top-level reassign) makes the resolver allow multiple to a variable
    80	// at top-level. It also allows if-, for-, and while-loops at top-level,
    81	// which in turn may make the evaluator dynamically assign multiple
    82	// values to a variable at top-level. (These two roles should be separated.)
    83	
    84	import (
    85	        "fmt"
    86	        "log"
    87	        "sort"
    88	        "strings"
    89	
    90	        "go.starlark.net/internal/spell"
    91	        "go.starlark.net/syntax"
    92	)
    93	
    94	const debug = false
    95	const doesnt = "this Starlark dialect does not "
    96	
    97	// global options
    98	// These features are either not standard Starlark (yet), or deprecated
    99	// features of the BUILD language, so we put them behind flags.
   100	//
   101	// Deprecated: use an explicit [syntax.FileOptions] argument instead,
   102	// as it avoids all the usual problems of global variables.
   103	var (
   104	        AllowSet            = false // allow the 'set' built-in
   105	        AllowGlobalReassign = false // allow reassignment to top-level names; also, allow if/for/while at top-level
   106	        AllowRecursion      = false // allow while statements and recursive functions
   107	        LoadBindsGlobally   = false // load creates global not file-local bindings (deprecated)
   108	
   109	        // obsolete flags for features that are now standard. No effect.
   110	        AllowNestedDef = true
   111	        AllowLambda    = true
   112	        AllowFloat     = true
   113	        AllowBitwise   = true
   114	)
   115	
   116	// File resolves the specified file and records information about the
   117	// module in file.Module.
   118	//
   119	// The isPredeclared and isUniversal predicates report whether a name is
   120	// a pre-declared identifier (visible in the current module) or a
   121	// universal identifier (visible in every module).
   122	// Clients should typically pass predeclared.Has for the first and
   123	// starlark.Universe.Has for the second, where predeclared is the
   124	// module's StringDict of predeclared names and starlark.Universe is the
   125	// standard set of built-ins.
   126	// The isUniverse predicate is supplied a parameter to avoid a cyclic
   127	// dependency upon starlark.Universe, not because users should ever need
   128	// to redefine it.
   129	func File(file *syntax.File, isPredeclared, isUniversal func(name string) bool) error {
   130	        return REPLChunk(file, nil, isPredeclared, isUniversal)
   131	}
   132	
   133	// REPLChunk is a generalization of the File function that supports a
   134	// non-empty initial global block, as occurs in a REPL.
   135	func REPLChunk(file *syntax.File, isGlobal, isPredeclared, isUniversal func(name string) bool) error {
   136	        r := newResolver(file.Options, isGlobal, isPredeclared, isUniversal)
   137	        r.stmts(file.Stmts)
   138	
   139	        r.env.resolveLocalUses()
   140	
   141	        // At the end of the module, resolve all non-local variable references,
   142	        // computing closures.
   143	        // Function bodies may contain forward references to later global declarations.
   144	        r.resolveNonLocalUses(r.env)
   145	
   146	        file.Module = &Module{
   147	                Locals:  r.moduleLocals,
   148	                Globals: r.moduleGlobals,
   149	        }
   150	
   151	        if len(r.errors) > 0 {
   152	                return r.errors
   153	        }
   154	        return nil
   155	}
   156	
   157	// Expr calls [ExprOptions] using [syntax.LegacyFileOptions].
   158	//
   159	// Deprecated: use [ExprOptions] with [syntax.FileOptions] instead,
   160	// because this function relies on legacy global variables.
   161	func Expr(expr syntax.Expr, isPredeclared, isUniversal func(name string) bool) ([]*Binding, error) {
   162	        return ExprOptions(syntax.LegacyFileOptions(), expr, isPredeclared, isUniversal)
   163	}
   164	
   165	// ExprOptions resolves the specified expression.
   166	// It returns the local variables bound within the expression.
   167	//
   168	// The isPredeclared and isUniversal predicates behave as for the File function
   169	func ExprOptions(opts *syntax.FileOptions, expr syntax.Expr, isPredeclared, isUniversal func(name string) bool) ([]*Binding, error) {
   170	        r := newResolver(opts, nil, isPredeclared, isUniversal)
   171	        r.expr(expr)
   172	        r.env.resolveLocalUses()
   173	        r.resolveNonLocalUses(r.env) // globals & universals
   174	        if len(r.errors) > 0 {
   175	                return nil, r.errors
   176	        }
   177	        return r.moduleLocals, nil
   178	}
   179	
   180	// An ErrorList is a non-empty list of resolver error messages.
   181	type ErrorList []Error // len > 0
   182	
   183	func (e ErrorList) Error() string { return e[0].Error() }
   184	
   185	// An Error describes the nature and position of a resolver error.
   186	type Error struct {
   187	        Pos syntax.Position
   188	        Msg string
   189	}
   190	
   191	func (e Error) Error() string { return e.Pos.String() + ": " + e.Msg }
   192	
   193	func newResolver(options *syntax.FileOptions, isGlobal, isPredeclared, isUniversal func(name string) bool) *resolver {
   194	        file := new(block)
   195	        return &resolver{
   196	                options:       options,
   197	                file:          file,
   198	                env:           file,
   199	                isGlobal:      isGlobal,
   200	                isPredeclared: isPredeclared,
   201	                isUniversal:   isUniversal,
   202	                globals:       make(map[string]*Binding),
   203	                predeclared:   make(map[string]*Binding),
   204	        }
   205	}
   206	
   207	type resolver struct {
   208	        options *syntax.FileOptions
   209	
   210	        // env is the current local environment:
   211	        // a linked list of blocks, innermost first.
   212	        // The tail of the list is the file block.
   213	        env  *block
   214	        file *block // file block (contains load bindings)
   215	
   216	        // moduleLocals contains the local variables of the module
   217	        // (due to load statements and comprehensions outside any function).
   218	        // moduleGlobals contains the global variables of the module.
   219	        moduleLocals  []*Binding
   220	        moduleGlobals []*Binding
   221	
   222	        // globals maps each global name in the module to its binding.
   223	        // predeclared does the same for predeclared and universal names.
   224	        globals     map[string]*Binding
   225	        predeclared map[string]*Binding
   226	
   227	        // These predicates report whether a name is
   228	        // pre-declared, either in this module or universally,
   229	        // or already declared in the module globals (as in a REPL).
   230	        // isGlobal may be nil.
   231	        isGlobal, isPredeclared, isUniversal func(name string) bool
   232	
   233	        loops   int // number of enclosing for/while loops
   234	        ifstmts int // number of enclosing if statements loops
   235	
   236	        errors ErrorList
   237	}
   238	
   239	// container returns the innermost enclosing "container" block:
   240	// a function (function != nil) or file (function == nil).
   241	// Container blocks accumulate local variable bindings.
   242	func (r *resolver) container() *block {
   243	        for b := r.env; ; b = b.parent {
   244	                if b.function != nil || b == r.file {
   245	                        return b
   246	                }
   247	        }
   248	}
   249	
   250	func (r *resolver) push(b *block) {
   251	        r.env.children = append(r.env.children, b)
   252	        b.parent = r.env
   253	        r.env = b
   254	}
   255	
   256	func (r *resolver) pop() { r.env = r.env.parent }
   257	
   258	type block struct {
   259	        parent *block // nil for file block
   260	
   261	        // In the file (root) block, both these fields are nil.
   262	        function *Function             // only for function blocks
   263	        comp     *syntax.Comprehension // only for comprehension blocks
   264	
   265	        // bindings maps a name to its binding.
   266	        // A local binding has an index into its innermost enclosing container's locals array.
   267	        // A free binding has an index into its innermost enclosing function's freevars array.
   268	        bindings map[string]*Binding
   269	
   270	        // children records the child blocks of the current one.
   271	        children []*block
   272	
   273	        // uses records all identifiers seen in this container (function or file),
   274	        // and a reference to the environment in which they appear.
   275	        // As we leave each container block, we resolve them,
   276	        // so that only free and global ones remain.
   277	        // At the end of each top-level function we compute closures.
   278	        uses []use
   279	}
   280	
   281	func (b *block) bind(name string, bind *Binding) {
   282	        if b.bindings == nil {
   283	                b.bindings = make(map[string]*Binding)
   284	        }
   285	        b.bindings[name] = bind
   286	}
   287	
   288	func (b *block) String() string {
   289	        if b.function != nil {
   290	                return "function block at " + fmt.Sprint(b.function.Pos)
   291	        }
   292	        if b.comp != nil {
   293	                return "comprehension block at " + fmt.Sprint(b.comp.Span())
   294	        }
   295	        return "file block"
   296	}
   297	
   298	func (r *resolver) errorf(posn syntax.Position, format string, args ...interface{}) {
   299	        r.errors = append(r.errors, Error{posn, fmt.Sprintf(format, args...)})
   300	}
   301	
   302	// A use records an identifier and the environment in which it appears.
   303	type use struct {
   304	        id  *syntax.Ident
   305	        env *block
   306	}
   307	
   308	// bind creates a binding for id: a global (not file-local)
   309	// binding at top-level, a local binding otherwise.
   310	// At top-level, it reports an error if a global or file-local
   311	// binding already exists, unless AllowGlobalReassign.
   312	// It sets id.Binding to the binding (whether old or new),
   313	// and returns whether a binding already existed.
   314	func (r *resolver) bind(id *syntax.Ident) bool {
   315	        // Binding outside any local (comprehension/function) block?
   316	        if r.env == r.file {
   317	                bind, ok := r.file.bindings[id.Name]
   318	                if !ok {
   319	                        bind, ok = r.globals[id.Name]
   320	                        if !ok {
   321	                                // first global binding of this name
   322	                                bind = &Binding{
   323	                                        First: id,
   324	                                        Scope: Global,
   325	                                        Index: len(r.moduleGlobals),
   326	                                }
   327	                                r.globals[id.Name] = bind
   328	                                r.moduleGlobals = append(r.moduleGlobals, bind)
   329	                        }
   330	                }
   331	                if ok && !r.options.GlobalReassign {
   332	                        r.errorf(id.NamePos, "cannot reassign %s %s declared at %s",
   333	                                bind.Scope, id.Name, bind.First.NamePos)
   334	                }
   335	                id.Binding = bind
   336	                return ok
   337	        }
   338	
   339	        return r.bindLocal(id)
   340	}
   341	
   342	func (r *resolver) bindLocal(id *syntax.Ident) bool {
   343	        // Mark this name as local to current block.
   344	        // Assign it a new local (positive) index in the current container.
   345	        _, ok := r.env.bindings[id.Name]
   346	        if !ok {
   347	                var locals *[]*Binding
   348	                if fn := r.container().function; fn != nil {
   349	                        locals = &fn.Locals
   350	                } else {
   351	                        locals = &r.moduleLocals
   352	                }
   353	                bind := &Binding{
   354	                        First: id,
   355	                        Scope: Local,
   356	                        Index: len(*locals),
   357	                }
   358	                r.env.bind(id.Name, bind)
   359	                *locals = append(*locals, bind)
   360	        }
   361	
   362	        r.use(id)
   363	        return ok
   364	}
   365	
   366	func (r *resolver) use(id *syntax.Ident) {
   367	        use := use{id, r.env}
   368	
   369	        // The spec says that if there is a global binding of a name
   370	        // then all references to that name in that block refer to the
   371	        // global, even if the use precedes the def---just as for locals.
   372	        // For example, in this code,
   373	        //
   374	        //   print(len); len=1; print(len)
   375	        //
   376	        // both occurrences of len refer to the len=1 binding, which
   377	        // completely shadows the predeclared len function.
   378	        //
   379	        // The rationale for these semantics, which differ from Python,
   380	        // is that the static meaning of len (a reference to a global)
   381	        // does not change depending on where it appears in the file.
   382	        // Of course, its dynamic meaning does change, from an error
   383	        // into a valid reference, so it's not clear these semantics
   384	        // have any practical advantage.
   385	        //
   386	        // In any case, the Bazel implementation lags behind the spec
   387	        // and follows Python behavior, so the first use of len refers
   388	        // to the predeclared function.  This typically used in a BUILD
   389	        // file that redefines a predeclared name half way through,
   390	        // for example:
   391	        //
   392	        //      proto_library(...)                      # built-in rule
   393	        //      load("myproto.bzl", "proto_library")
   394	        //      proto_library(...)                      # user-defined rule
   395	        //
   396	        // We will piggyback support for the legacy semantics on the
   397	        // AllowGlobalReassign flag, which is loosely related and also
   398	        // required for Bazel.
   399	        if r.options.GlobalReassign && r.env == r.file {
   400	                r.useToplevel(use)
   401	                return
   402	        }

2025-12-30 00:58:19,355 - INFO - swea-agent - 💭 THOUGHT
Now I understand the issue! The resolver checks if `break` or `continue` is in a loop at line 505 by checking if `r.loops == 0`. However, when processing a nested function definition, the function creates a new scope, but the `r.loops` counter is shared across the resolver. This means:

1. When we enter a `for` loop, `r.loops` is incremented.
2. When we define a nested function inside that loop, we call `r.function()`.
3. Inside `r.function()`, we call `r.stmts()` to process the function body.
4. At this point, `r.loops` is still > 0 (inherited from the outer context).
5. So when we encounter a `break` or `continue` inside the nested function, the check at line 505 passes incorrectly because `r.loops > 0`.

The fix is to save and restore the `r.loops` count when entering and leaving a function scope. Let me check if there's a similar issue with `r.ifstmts`:

Looking at the code, I can see that both `r.loops` and `r.ifstmts` are counters that track the enclosing context. When we enter a function, we should reset these counters because a nested function is a new scope and break/continue statements should not be able to reference loops outside the function.

Let me create a test script to reproduce the error first:

      break

When we enter a function, we should reset the `r.loops` counter (and probably `r.ifstmts` too for consistency), and restore them when we exit:

   813	func (r *resolver) function(function *Function, pos syntax.Position) {
   814	        // Resolve defaults in enclosing environment.
   815	        for _, param := range function.Params {
   816	                if binary, ok := param.(*syntax.BinaryExpr); ok {
   817	                        r.expr(binary.Y)
   818	                }
   819	        }
   820	
   821	        // Enter function block.
   822	        b := &block{function: function}
   823	        r.push(b)
   824	
   825	        var seenOptional bool
   826	        var star *syntax.UnaryExpr // * or *args param
   827	        var starStar *syntax.Ident // **kwargs ident
   828	        var numKwonlyParams int
   829	        for _, param := range function.Params {
   830	                switch param := param.(type) {
   831	                case *syntax.Ident:
   832	                        // e.g. x
   833	                        if starStar != nil {
   834	                                r.errorf(param.NamePos, "required parameter may not follow **%s", starStar.Name)
   835	                        } else if star != nil {
   836	                                numKwonlyParams++
   837	                        } else if seenOptional {
   838	                                r.errorf(param.NamePos, "required parameter may not follow optional")
   839	                        }
   840	                        if r.bind(param) {
   841	                                r.errorf(param.NamePos, "duplicate parameter: %s", param.Name)
   842	                        }
   843	
   844	                case *syntax.BinaryExpr:
   845	                        // e.g. y=dflt
   846	                        if starStar != nil {
   847	                                r.errorf(param.OpPos, "optional parameter may not follow **%s", starStar.Name)
   848	                        } else if star != nil {
   849	                                numKwonlyParams++
   850	                        }
   851	                        if id := param.X.(*syntax.Ident); r.bind(id) {
   852	                                r.errorf(param.OpPos, "duplicate parameter: %s", id.Name)
   853	                        }
   854	                        seenOptional = true
   855	
   856	                case *syntax.UnaryExpr:
   857	                        // * or *args or **kwargs
   858	                        if param.Op == syntax.STAR {
   859	                                if starStar != nil {
   860	                                        r.errorf(param.OpPos, "* parameter may not follow **%s", starStar.Name)
   861	                                } else if star != nil {
   862	                                        r.errorf(param.OpPos, "multiple * parameters not allowed")
   863	                                } else {
   864	                                        star = param
   865	                                }
   866	                        } else {
   867	                                if starStar != nil {
   868	                                        r.errorf(param.OpPos, "multiple ** parameters not allowed")
   869	                                }
   870	                                starStar = param.X.(*syntax.Ident)
   871	                        }
   872	                }
   873	        }
   874	
   875	        // Bind the *args and **kwargs parameters at the end,
   876	        // so that regular parameters a/b/c are contiguous and
   877	        // there is no hole for the "*":
   878	        //   def f(a, b, *args, c=0, **kwargs)
   879	        //   def f(a, b, *,     c=0, **kwargs)
   880	        if star != nil {
   881	                if id, _ := star.X.(*syntax.Ident); id != nil {
   882	                        // *args
   883	                        if r.bind(id) {
   884	                                r.errorf(id.NamePos, "duplicate parameter: %s", id.Name)
   885	                        }
   886	                        function.HasVarargs = true
   887	                } else if numKwonlyParams == 0 {
   888	                        r.errorf(star.OpPos, "bare * must be followed by keyword-only parameters")
   889	                }
   890	        }
   891	        if starStar != nil {
   892	                if r.bind(starStar) {
   893	                        r.errorf(starStar.NamePos, "duplicate parameter: %s", starStar.Name)
   894	                }
   895	                function.HasKwargs = true
   896	        }
   897	
   898	        function.NumKwonlyParams = numKwonlyParams
   899	        r.stmts(function.Body)
   900	
   901	        // Resolve all uses of this function's local vars,
   902	        // and keep just the remaining uses of free/global vars.
   903	        b.resolveLocalUses()
   904	
   905	        // Leave function block.
   906	        r.pop()
   907	
   908	        // References within the function body to globals are not
   909	        // resolved until the end of the module.
   910	}

    30	        return strings.Contains(chunk, "option:"+name)
    31	}
    32	
    33	func TestResolve(t *testing.T) {
    34	        filename := starlarktest.DataFile("resolve", "testdata/resolve.star")
    35	        for _, chunk := range chunkedfile.Read(filename, t) {
    36	                // A chunk may set options by containing e.g. "option:recursion".
    37	                opts := getOptions(chunk.Source)
    38	
    39	                f, err := opts.Parse(filename, chunk.Source, 0)
    40	                if err != nil {
    41	                        t.Error(err)
    42	                        continue
    43	                }
    44	
    45	                if err := resolve.File(f, isPredeclared, isUniversal); err != nil {
    46	                        for _, err := range err.(resolve.ErrorList) {
    47	                                chunk.GotError(int(err.Pos.Line), err.Msg)
    48	                        }
    49	                }
    50	                chunk.Done()
    51	        }
    52	}

    54	func TestDefVarargsAndKwargsSet(t *testing.T) {
    55	        source := "def f(*args, **kwargs): pass\n"
    56	        file, err := syntax.Parse("foo.star", source, 0)
    57	        if err != nil {
    58	                t.Fatal(err)
    59	        }
    60	        if err := resolve.File(file, isPredeclared, isUniversal); err != nil {
    61	                t.Fatal(err)
    62	        }
    63	        fn := file.Stmts[0].(*syntax.DefStmt).Function.(*resolve.Function)
    64	        if !fn.HasVarargs {
    65	                t.Error("HasVarargs not set")
    66	        }
    67	        if !fn.HasKwargs {
    68	                t.Error("HasKwargs not set")
    69	        }
    70	}

🎬 ACTION
str_replace_editor create /testbed/test_comprehensive.star --file_text '# Comprehensive test for break/continue in nested functions

# Test 1: Valid break/continue in loops
def test1():
    result = []
    for i in [1, 2, 3, 4, 5]:
        if i == 3:
            continue
        if i == 5:
            break
        result.append(i)
    return result

assert.eq(test1(), [1, 2, 4])

# Test 2: Valid break/continue in nested function'"'"'s own loop
def test2():
    def inner():
        result = []
        for j in [10, 20, 30, 40]:
            if j == 20:
                continue
            if j == 40:
                break
            result.append(j)
        return result
    return inner()

assert.eq(test2(), [10, 30])

# Test 3: Multiple levels of nesting with valid break/continue
def test3():
    def level1():
        result = []
        for i in [1, 2]:
            def level2():
                inner_result = []
                for j in [10, 20]:
                    if j == 20:
                        break
                    inner_result.append(j)
                return inner_result
            result.extend(level2())
        return result
    return level1()

assert.eq(test3(), [10, 10])

# Test 4: break/continue work correctly in lambdas inside loops
def test4():
    result = []
    for i in [1, 2, 3]:
        # Lambda can reference the loop variable but can'"'"'t use break/continue
        f = lambda x: x + i
        result.append(f(10))
    return result

assert.eq(test4(), [11, 12, 13])

print("All tests passed!")

# Test 1: Valid break/continue in loops
def test1():
    result = []
    for i in [1, 2, 3, 4, 5]:
        if i == 3:
            continue
        if i == 5:
            break
        result.append(i)
    return result

assert.eq(test1(), [1, 2, 4])

# Test 2: Valid break/continue in nested function'"'"'s own loop
def test2():
    def inner():
        result = []
        for j in [10, 20, 30, 40]:
            if j == 20:
                continue
            if j == 40:
                break
            result.append(j)
        return result
    return inner()

assert.eq(test2(), [10, 30])

# Test 3: Multiple levels of nesting with valid break/continue
def test3():
    def level1():
        result = []
        for i in [1, 2]:
            def level2():
                inner_result = []
                for j in [10, 20]:
                    if j == 20:
                        break
                    inner_result.append(j)
                return inner_result
            result.extend(level2())
        return result
    return level1()

assert.eq(test3(), [10, 10])

# Test 4: break/continue work correctly in lambdas inside loops
def test4():
    result = []
    for i in [1, 2, 3]:
        # Lambda can reference the loop variable but can'"'"'t use break/continue
        f = lambda x: x + i
        result.append(f(10))
    return result

assert.eq(test4(), [11, 12, 13])

print("All tests passed!")' --new_str '# Comprehensive test for break/continue in nested functions

I see comprehensions also create a new block with `r.push(&block{comp: e})`, but they don't reset the loop counters. Let me verify this is working correctly by checking if there's already protection against break/continue in comprehensions:

Since break/continue are statements, not expressions, they can't actually appear inside comprehension bodies (which only contain expressions). The parser would reject them, as we saw earlier. So comprehensions are safe.

# Test suite for break/continue in nested functions

echo "Test 1: break in nested function (should fail with error)"
cat > test1.star << '"'"'EOF'"'"'
def fun():
  for a in [1, 2, 3]:
    def nested():
      break
fun()
EOF
go run ./cmd/starlark test1.star 2>&1 | grep -q "break not in a loop" && echo "PASS: Test 1" || echo "FAIL: Test 1"

echo ""
echo "Test 2: continue in nested function (should fail with error)"
cat > test2.star << '"'"'EOF'"'"'
def fun():
  for a in [1, 2, 3]:
    def nested():
      continue
fun()
EOF
go run ./cmd/starlark test2.star 2>&1 | grep -q "continue not in a loop" && echo "PASS: Test 2" || echo "FAIL: Test 2"

echo ""
echo "Test 3: break in deeply nested function (should fail with error)"
cat > test3.star << '"'"'EOF'"'"'
def level1():
  for i in [1, 2]:
    def level2():
      for j in [10, 20]:
        def level3():
          break
        level3()
    level2()
level1()
EOF
go run ./cmd/starlark test3.star 2>&1 | grep -q "break not in a loop" && echo "PASS: Test 3" || echo "FAIL: Test 3"

echo ""
echo "Test 4: Valid break/continue in nested function'"'"'s own loop (should succeed)"
cat > test4.star << '"'"'EOF'"'"'
def outer():
    for i in [1, 2, 3]:
        print("outer", i)
    
    def inner():
        for j in [10, 20, 30]:
            if j == 20:
                continue
            print("inner", j)
    
    inner()

outer()
EOF
go run ./cmd/starlark test4.star 2>&1 | grep -q "inner 10" && go run ./cmd/starlark test4.star 2>&1 | grep -q "inner 30" && echo "PASS: Test 4" || echo "FAIL: Test 4"

echo ""
echo "Test 5: Valid break in outer function loop (should succeed)"
cat > test5.star << '"'"'EOF'"'"'
def test():
    for i in [1, 2, 3, 4, 5]:
        if i == 3:
            break
        print(i)
    print("done")
test()
EOF
go run ./cmd/starlark test5.star 2>&1 | grep -q "done" && echo "PASS: Test 5" || echo "FAIL: Test 5"

echo ""
echo "Test 6: continue without loop (should fail with error)"
cat > test6.star << '"'"'EOF'"'"'
def fun():
  def nested():
    continue
fun()
EOF
go run ./cmd/starlark test6.star 2>&1 | grep -q "continue not in a loop" && echo "PASS: Test 6" || echo "FAIL: Test 6"

echo ""
echo "All tests completed!"

# Cleanup
rm -f test1.star test2.star test3.star test4.star test5.star test6.star
'

2025-12-30 01:06:44,072 - INFO - swea-agent - 💭 THOUGHT
Perfect! Let me also verify that the fix is minimal and correct. The change we made:

1. **Problem**: When entering a nested function inside a loop, the `r.loops` counter was still > 0, so `break`/`continue` statements inside the nested function were incorrectly allowed.

2. **Solution**: When entering a function (via `r.function()`), we save the current `r.loops` and `r.ifstmts` counters, reset them to 0 for the function body, and then restore them when exiting the function. This ensures that break/continue statements inside the nested function only see the loops within that function, not loops in enclosing functions.

3. **Why it's correct**: 
   - Functions create a new lexical scope for control flow
   - A `break` or `continue` in a nested function should not be able to reference loops in an outer function
   - The fix ensures that the loop counter reflects only the loops in the current function's scope

4. **Why it's minimal**:
   - We only added 12 lines of code (including comments)
   - We used a defer statement to ensure cleanup happens even if there's an error
   - We didn't change the logic anywhere else
   - The change is localized to the function entry/exit point

For example:\n\n```starlark\ndef fun():\n  for a in [1, 2, 3]:\n    def nested():\n      break  # This caused a panic instead of an error\nfun()\n```\n\n### Root Cause\nThe resolver maintains counters (`r.loops` and `r.ifstmts`) to track the depth of loops and if-statements in the current scope. When processing a nested function, the resolver would enter the function scope but keep the parent\'s loop counter values. This meant that a `break` or `continue` statement inside the nested function would pass the validation check (which verifies `r.loops > 0`), but then the compiler would try to access a non-existent loop context, causing an index out of range panic.\n\n### Solution\nIn the `resolver.function()` method in `/testbed/resolve/resolve.go`, we now save the current `r.loops` and `r.ifstmts` counters when entering a function, reset them to 0 for the function body, and restore them when exiting. +        // The spec says that if there is a global binding of a name
+        // then all references to that name in that block refer to the
+        // global, even if the use precedes the def---just as for locals.
+        // For example, in this code,
+        //
+        //   print(len); len=1; print(len)
+        //
+        // both occurrences of len refer to the len=1 binding, which
+        // completely shadows the predeclared len function.
+        //
+        // The rationale for these semantics, which differ from Python,
+        // is that the static meaning of len (a reference to a global)
+        // does not change depending on where it appears in the file.
+        // Of course, its dynamic meaning does change, from an error
+        // into a valid reference, so it's not clear these semantics
+        // have any practical advantage.
+        //
+        // In any case, the Bazel implementation lags behind the spec
+        // and follows Python behavior, so the first use of len refers
+        // to the predeclared function.  This typically used in a BUILD
+        // file that redefines a predeclared name half way through,
+        // for example:

-				// Sadly we can't report the previous declaration

-				r.errorf(id.NamePos, "cannot reassign top-level %s", id.Name)
-			}
-		}
-
-	default:
-		log.Panicf("unexpected stmt %T", stmt)
-	}
+        switch stmt := stmt.(type) {
+        case *syntax.ExprStmt:
+                r.expr(stmt.X)
+
+        case *syntax.BranchStmt:
+                if r.loops == 0 && (stmt.Token == syntax.BREAK || stmt.Token == syntax.CONTINUE) {
+                        r.errorf(stmt.TokenPos, "%s not in a loop", stmt.Token)
+                }
+
+        case *syntax.IfStmt:
+                if !r.options.TopLevelControl && r.container().function == nil {
+                        r.errorf(stmt.If, "if statement not within a function")
+                }
+                r.expr(stmt.Cond)
+                r.ifstmts++
+                r.stmts(stmt.True)
+                r.stmts(stmt.False)
+                r.ifstmts--
+
+        case *syntax.AssignStmt:
+                r.expr(stmt.RHS)
+                isAugmented := stmt.Op != syntax.EQ
+                r.assign(stmt.LHS, isAugmented)
+
+        case *syntax.DefStmt:
+                r.bind(stmt.Name)
+                fn := &Function{
+                        Name:   stmt.Name.Name,
+                        Pos:    stmt.Def,
+                        Params: stmt.Params,
+                        Body:   stmt.Body,
+                }
+                stmt.Function = fn
+                r.function(fn, stmt.Def)
+
+        case *syntax.ForStmt:
+                if !r.options.TopLevelControl && r.container().function == nil {
+                        r.errorf(stmt.For, "for loop not within a function")
+                }
+                r.expr(stmt.X)
+                const isAugmented = false
+                r.assign(stmt.Vars, isAugmented)
+                r.loops++
+                r.stmts(stmt.Body)
+                r.loops--
+
+        case *syntax.WhileStmt:
+                if !r.options.While {
+                        r.errorf(stmt.While, doesnt+"support while loops")
+                }
+                if !r.options.TopLevelControl && r.container().function == nil {
+                        r.errorf(stmt.While, "while loop not within a function")
+                }
+                r.expr(stmt.Cond)
+                r.loops++
+                r.stmts(stmt.Body)
+                r.loops--
+
+        case *syntax.ReturnStmt:
+                if r.container().function == nil {
+                        r.errorf(stmt.Return, "return statement not within a function")
+                }
+                if stmt.Result != nil {
+                        r.expr(stmt.Result)
+                }
+
+        case *syntax.LoadStmt:
+                // A load statement may not be nested in any other statement.
+                if r.container().function != nil {
+                        r.errorf(stmt.Load, "load statement within a function")
+                } else if r.loops > 0 {
+                        r.errorf(stmt.Load, "load statement within a loop")
+                } else if r.ifstmts > 0 {
+                        r.errorf(stmt.Load, "load statement within a conditional")
+                }
+
+                for i, from := range stmt.From {
+                        if from.Name == "" {
+                                r.errorf(from.NamePos, "load: empty identifier")
+                                continue
+                        }
+                        if from.Name[0] == '_' {
+                                r.errorf(from.NamePos, "load: names with leading underscores are not exported: %s", from.Name)
+                        }
+
+                        id := stmt.To[i]
+                        if r.options.LoadBindsGlobally {
+                                r.bind(id)
+                        } else if r.bindLocal(id) && !r.options.GlobalReassign {
+                                // "Global" in AllowGlobalReassign is a misnomer for "toplevel".
+                                // Sadly we can't report the previous declaration
+                                // as id.Binding may not be set yet.
+                                r.errorf(id.NamePos, "cannot reassign top-level %s", id.Name)
+                        }
+                }
+
+        default:
+                log.Panicf("unexpected stmt %T", stmt)
+        }
 }

+                if isAugmented {
+                        r.errorf(syntax.Start(lhs), "can't use tuple expression in augmented assignment")

+                if isAugmented {
+                        r.errorf(syntax.Start(lhs), "can't use list expression in augmented assignment")
+                }
+                for _, elem := range lhs.List {
+                        r.assign(elem, isAugmented)
+                }
+
+        case *syntax.ParenExpr:
+                r.assign(lhs.X, isAugmented)
+
+        default:
+                name := strings.ToLower(strings.TrimPrefix(fmt.Sprintf("%T", lhs), "*syntax."))
+                r.errorf(syntax.Start(lhs), "can't assign to %s", name)
+        }

+                r.expr(e.False)

+                r.expr(e.Key)
+                r.expr(e.Value)

+        case *syntax.SliceExpr:
+                r.expr(e.X)
+                if e.Lo != nil {
+                        r.expr(e.Lo)
+                }
+                if e.Hi != nil {
+                        r.expr(e.Hi)
+                }
+                if e.Step != nil {
+                        r.expr(e.Step)
+                }
+
+        case *syntax.Comprehension:
+                // The 'in' operand of the first clause (always a ForClause)
+                // is resolved in the outer block; consider: [x for x in x].
+                clause := e.Clauses[0].(*syntax.ForClause)
+                r.expr(clause.X)
+
+                // A list/dict comprehension defines a new lexical block.
+                // Locals defined within the block will be allotted
+                // distinct slots in the locals array of the innermost
+                // enclosing container (function/module) block.
+                r.push(&block{comp: e})
+
+                const isAugmented = false
+                r.assign(clause.Vars, isAugmented)
+
+                for _, clause := range e.Clauses[1:] {

+                        case *syntax.ForClause:
+                                r.assign(clause.Vars, isAugmented)
+                                r.expr(clause.X)
+                        }
+                }
+                r.expr(e.Body) // body may be *DictEntry
+                r.pop()
+
+        case *syntax.TupleExpr:
+                for _, x := range e.List {
+                        r.expr(x)
+                }
+
+        case *syntax.DictExpr:
+                for _, entry := range e.List {
+                        entry := entry.(*syntax.DictEntry)
+                        r.expr(entry.Key)
+                        r.expr(entry.Value)
+                }
+
+        case *syntax.UnaryExpr:
+                r.expr(e.X)
+
+        case *syntax.BinaryExpr:
+                r.expr(e.X)
+                r.expr(e.Y)
+
+        case *syntax.DotExpr:
+                r.expr(e.X)
+                // ignore e.Name
+
+        case *syntax.CallExpr:
+                r.expr(e.Fn)
+                var seenVarargs, seenKwargs bool
+                var seenName map[string]bool
+                var n, p int
+                for _, arg := range e.Args {
+                        pos, _ := arg.Span()
+                        if unop, ok := arg.(*syntax.UnaryExpr); ok && unop.Op == syntax.STARSTAR {
+                                // **kwargs
+                                if seenKwargs {
+                                        r.errorf(pos, "multiple **kwargs not allowed")
+                                }
+                                seenKwargs = true
+                                r.expr(arg)
+                        } else if ok && unop.Op == syntax.STAR {
+                                // *args
+                                if seenKwargs {
+                                        r.errorf(pos, "*args may not follow **kwargs")
+                                } else if seenVarargs {
+                                        r.errorf(pos, "multiple *args not allowed")
+                                }
+                                seenVarargs = true
+                                r.expr(arg)
+                        } else if binop, ok := arg.(*syntax.BinaryExpr); ok && binop.Op == syntax.EQ {
+                                // k=v
+                                n++
+                                if seenKwargs {
+                                        r.errorf(pos, "keyword argument may not follow **kwargs")
+                                } else if seenVarargs {
+                                        r.errorf(pos, "keyword argument may not follow *args")
+                                }
+                                x := binop.X.(*syntax.Ident)
+                                if seenName[x.Name] {
+                                        r.errorf(x.NamePos, "keyword argument %q is repeated", x.Name)
+                                } else {
+                                        if seenName == nil {
+                                                seenName = make(map[string]bool)
+                                        }
+                                        seenName[x.Name] = true
+                                }
+                                r.expr(binop.Y)
+                        } else {
+                                // positional argument
+                                p++
+                                if seenVarargs {
+                                        r.errorf(pos, "positional argument may not follow *args")
+                                } else if seenKwargs {
+                                        r.errorf(pos, "positional argument may not follow **kwargs")
+                                } else if len(seenName) > 0 {
+                                        r.errorf(pos, "positional argument may not follow named")
+                                }

+                        }
+                }
+
+                // Fail gracefully if compiler-imposed limit is exceeded.

+                }

+                }

+
+        case *syntax.ParenExpr:
+                r.expr(e.X)
+
+        default:
+                log.Panicf("unexpected expr %T", e)
+        }

-	// References within the function body to globals are not

+        // Resolve defaults in enclosing environment.
+        for _, param := range function.Params {
+                if binary, ok := param.(*syntax.BinaryExpr); ok {
+                        r.expr(binary.Y)
+                }
+        }
+
+        // Enter function block.
+        b := &block{function: function}
+        r.push(b)
+
+        // A new function establishes a new lexical block for control flow.
+        // Save and restore the loop/ifstmt counts to ensure break/continue
+        // are only allowed within loops in the current function, not
+        // referring to loops in enclosing functions.
+        savedLoops := r.loops
+        savedIfstmts := r.ifstmts
+        r.loops = 0
+        r.ifstmts = 0
+        defer func() {
+                r.loops = savedLoops
+                r.ifstmts = savedIfstmts
+        }()
+
+        var seenOptional bool
+        var star *syntax.UnaryExpr // * or *args param
+        var starStar *syntax.Ident // **kwargs ident
+        var numKwonlyParams int
+        for _, param := range function.Params {
+                switch param := param.(type) {
+                case *syntax.Ident:
+                        // e.g. x
+                        if starStar != nil {
+                                r.errorf(param.NamePos, "required parameter may not follow **%s", starStar.Name)
+                        } else if star != nil {
+                                numKwonlyParams++
+                        } else if seenOptional {
+                                r.errorf(param.NamePos, "required parameter may not follow optional")
+                        }
+                        if r.bind(param) {
+                                r.errorf(param.NamePos, "duplicate parameter: %s", param.Name)
+                        }
+
+                case *syntax.BinaryExpr:
+                        // e.g. y=dflt
+                        if starStar != nil {
+                                r.errorf(param.OpPos, "optional parameter may not follow **%s", starStar.Name)
+                        } else if star != nil {
+                                numKwonlyParams++

+                        if id := param.X.(*syntax.Ident); r.bind(id) {
+                                r.errorf(param.OpPos, "duplicate parameter: %s", id.Name)
+                        }
+                        seenOptional = true
+
+                case *syntax.UnaryExpr:
+                        // * or *args or **kwargs
+                        if param.Op == syntax.STAR {
+                                if starStar != nil {
+                                        r.errorf(param.OpPos, "* parameter may not follow **%s", starStar.Name)
+                                } else if star != nil {
+                                        r.errorf(param.OpPos, "multiple * parameters not allowed")
+                                } else {
+                                        star = param
+                                }
+                        } else {
+                                if starStar != nil {
+                                        r.errorf(param.OpPos, "multiple ** parameters not allowed")
+                                }
+                                starStar = param.X.(*syntax.Ident)
+                        }
+                }
+        }
+
+        // Bind the *args and **kwargs parameters at the end,
+        // so that regular parameters a/b/c are contiguous and
+        // there is no hole for the "*":
+        //   def f(a, b, *args, c=0, **kwargs)
+        //   def f(a, b, *,     c=0, **kwargs)
+        if star != nil {
+                if id, _ := star.X.(*syntax.Ident); id != nil {
+                        // *args
+                        if r.bind(id) {
+                                r.errorf(id.NamePos, "duplicate parameter: %s", id.Name)
+                        }
+                        function.HasVarargs = true
+                } else if numKwonlyParams == 0 {
+                        r.errorf(star.OpPos, "bare * must be followed by keyword-only parameters")
+                }
+        }
+        if starStar != nil {
+                if r.bind(starStar) {
+                        r.errorf(starStar.NamePos, "duplicate parameter: %s", starStar.Name)
+                }
+                function.HasKwargs = true
+        }
+
+        function.NumKwonlyParams = numKwonlyParams
+        r.stmts(function.Body)
+
+        // Resolve all uses of this function's local vars,
+        // and keep just the remaining uses of free/global vars.
+        b.resolveLocalUses()
+
+        // Leave function block.
+        r.pop()
+
+        // References within the function body to globals are not
+        // resolved until the end of the module.
 }
 
 func (r *resolver) resolveNonLocalUses(b *block) {
-	// First resolve inner blocks.
-	for _, child := range b.children {
-		r.resolveNonLocalUses(child)
-	}
-	for _, use := range b.uses {
-		use.id.Binding = r.lookupLexical(use, use.env)
-	}
+        // First resolve inner blocks.
+        for _, child := range b.children {
+                r.resolveNonLocalUses(child)
+        }
+        for _, use := range b.uses {
+                use.id.Binding = r.lookupLexical(use, use.env)
+        }
 }

#!/usr/bin/env python3

with open('/testbed/resolve/resolve.go', 'r') as f:
    lines = f.readlines()

# Find the line after "r.push(b)" in the function method
insert_after = None
for i, line in enumerate(lines):
    if i >= 820 and 'r.push(b)' in line and 'block{function: function}' in lines[i-1]:
        insert_after = i
        break

if insert_after is None:
    print("Could not find insertion point")
    exit(1)

# The new code to insert (using tabs for indentation)
new_code = [
    '\n',
    '\t// A new function establishes a new lexical block for control flow.\n',
    '\t// Save and restore the loop/ifstmt counts to ensure break/continue\n',
    '\t// are only allowed within loops in the current function, not\n',
    '\t// referring to loops in enclosing functions.\n',
    '\tsavedLoops := r.loops\n',
    '\tsavedIfstmts := r.ifstmts\n',
    '\tr.loops = 0\n',
    '\tr.ifstmts = 0\n',
    '\tdefer func() {\n',
    '\t\tr.loops = savedLoops\n',
    '\t\tr.ifstmts = savedIfstmts\n',
    '\t}()\n',
]

# Insert the new code
lines[insert_after+1:insert_after+1] = new_code

# Write the file back
with open('/testbed/resolve/resolve.go', 'w') as f:
    f.writelines(lines)

print(f"Inserted code after line {insert_after}")
EOF
